Jamison Brereton

11 (202)
Indra
Gr╠еtsamada
21 verses: vir─Бс╣нsth─Бn─Б triс╣гс╣нubh, except triс╣гс╣нubh 21
Judging from its frequent references to the winds, this Indra hymn was composed to accompany the dayтАЩs first soma-pressing, which anciently belonged especially to Indra and V─Бyu, the Wind. It is also a good example of the complexity of R╠еgvedic poetry. The poet uses ellipses and ambiguous reference to suggest the union of the acts of the accompanying ritual and the action of the myth. In verse 3, for example, the тАЬresplendentтАЭ (┼Ыubhr├б) ones who run to the wind are the Maruts, the gods who so often accompany Indra. But the adjective тАЬresplendentтАЭ is also used of soma, and therefore the verse carries a second, suggested meaning that the offering of soma goes to the Wind, who receives the soma along with Indra. Or again, in verses 7тАУ8, it appears at first as though the mountain described there is one of the mountains settled by Indra when he made the world habitable. But this mountain is described in odd ways: it does not falter; it bellows with its mothers; and it roarsтАФ descriptions that force a reconsideration of its identity. Elsewhere these epithets characterize the fire, which is тАЬsettledтАЭ by priests on the sacrificial area. Thus, the creative actions of the god and the ritual actions of the priests are placed in parallel and made reflexes of one another. For a detailed analysis of this hymn, which seeks to demonstrate its double reference to myth and ritual, see Brereton (1985).

Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra [II.11-24 JPB] [II.11 Indra (misc. comments by SJ to JPB tr.)

The hymn has a remarkable number of predicated tense-stem participles.

Another notable feature is the large number of occurrences of the particle n├║, all in the first p─Бda of the vs., in short runs of adjacent vss.: 3a, 4a; 6a, 7a; 15a, 16a, 17a. The last vs. of the hymn (21) then begins n┼лn├бm, as if in summary.

On the unusual meter of this hymn see Oldenberg Prol. 87-90, who also remarks on its unusual vocab., which, taken together, gives the hymn a тАЬSonderstellungтАЭ among the surrounding hymns (87 n. 1).

рдЧреГрддреНрд╕рдорджрдГрд╕реНрддреМрддрд┐ рд╣реЗрдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рдореЗрд╣рд╡рдореНрдорджреАрдпрдорд┐рджрдВрд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░рдВ рд╢реНрд░реБрдзрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реГрдгреБ рдорд╛рд░рд┐рд╖рдгреНрдпрдГ рдорд╛рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕реАрдГ рдЗрджрдорд▓реНрдкрдВ рдирд╕рд╛рдзреА- рдпрдЗрддрд┐рдорд╛рдирд┐рд░рд╛рдХрд╛рд░реНрд╖реАрдГ рджреБрд░рд╕реНрдпреБрд░реНрджреНрд░рд╡рд┐рдгрд╕реНрдпреБрд░реНрд╡реГрд╖рдгреНрдпрддрд┐рд░рд┐рд╖рдгреНрдпрддреАрддрд┐рдирд┐рдкрд╛рддрд┐рддрдГ рд╡рдпрдиреНрддреЗрддрд╡рд╡рд╕реВрдирд╛рдиреНрджрд╛рд╡рдиреЗрджрд╛рдирд╛рдп- рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдордкрд╛рддреНрд░рднреВрддрд╛рднрд╡реЗрдо рдЗрдорд╛рдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рднрд┐рд░реНрджрддреНрддрд╛рдирд┐рд╡рд╕реВрдпрд╡рдГ рджрд╛рддреБрд░реНрдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдпрдзрдирдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ рдЫрдиреНрджрд╕рд┐рдкрд░реЗрдЪреНрдЫрд╛- рдпрд╛рдЩреНрдХреНрдпрдЪреН рддрд╛рджреГрд╢рд╛рдирд┐рдХреНрд╖рд░рдиреНрддрдГ рд╕реНрд░рд╡рдиреНрддрдГ рд╕рд┐рдиреНрдзрд╡рдЗрд╡ рдШреГрддрдХреНрд╖рд░рдгреЛрдкреЗрддрд╛рдирд┐рдКрд░реНрдЬреЛрд╣рд╡рд┐рд░реНрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рдиреНрдпрдиреНрдирд╛рдирд┐ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╡рдпрд░реНрдз- рдиреНрддрд┐рд╣рд┐ рее рез рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, hear (my) invocation; disregard it not; may we be (thought worthy) of the gift of your treasures; these oblations, designed to obtain wealth, flowing (abundantly) like rivers, bring to you augmented vigour.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Hear our summons, Indra! Intend us no harm! We would be those to be given good things by you.
For these nourishments, like flowing rivers, strengthen you in their quest for good things.

Griffith

HEAR thou my call, O Indra; be not heedless: thine may we be for thee to give us treasures;
For these presented viands, seeking riches, increase thy strength like streams of water flowing.

Geldner

Grassmann

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, hero, you have set free the copious (waters) which were formerly arrested by Ahi, and which you have distributed; invogorated by hymns, you have cast down headlong the slave, conceiting himself immortal.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You let loose the great (waters), Indra, which you swelledтАФthe many (waters) surrounded by the serpent [=Vr╠еtra], o champion.
You cut down the D─Бsa [=Vr╠еtra], even though he thought he was
immortal, when you became strong through the hymns.414 II.11

Jamison Brereton Notes

The pf. part. v─Бvс╣Ыdh─Бn├бс╕е would better be rendered as an anterior: тАЬwhen you had become strong тАжтАЭ

Griffith

Floods great and many, compassed by the Dragon, thou badest swell and settest free, O Hero.
Strengthened by songs of praise thou rentest piecemeal the Dasa, him who deemed himself immortal.

Geldner

Du lie├Яest die gro├Яem Str├╢me laufen, o Indra, die du anschwelltest, die vielen von dem Drachen umstellten, du Held. Den Dasa, der sich sogar f├╝r einen Unsterblichen hielt, hiebst du herunter, durch die Loblieder aufgerichtet.

Grassmann

Du liessest frei die Str├╢me, die du schwelltest, die vielen, Indra, von der Schlang’ umstellten; Den D├дmon auch, der sich unsterblich d├╝nkte, schlugst du herab, durch Spr├╝che wohlgekr├дftigt.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, hero, these brilliant (laudations), in (the form of) hymns, in which you delight, and in (that of) the praises uttered by the worshipper by which you are gratified, are addressed to you, to bring you (to your sacrifice).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

In the praises uttered by the worshippers: rudriyeс╣гu stomeс╣гu: rudriya = the means of giving plural asure, sukhas─Бdhana bh┼лteс╣гu;or, rudraс╕е = stot─Бraс╕е, praisers, worshipped

Jamison Brereton

(Delight) now in just these hymns in which you delight, o champion, and in Rudrian praise songs, Indra.
These (waters), in which you are finding exhilaration, run forth just to you as the resplendent ones (run forth) to the Wind [=V─Бyu].

Jamison Brereton Notes

There are several syntactic problems in this verse. The easiest to deal with is the apparently misplaced ca in b. All the standard tr. as well as the published translation take rudr├нyeс╣гu as a modifier of st├│meс╣гu, with the whole loc. phrase #ukth├йс╣гu тАж, st├│meс╣гu тАж rudr├нyeс╣гu ca# then interpreted as тАЬin the hymns and in the Rudriyan praises,тАЭ with the ca following the 2nd word of a bipartite NP and at a considerable distance from the 1st . (We would expect *st├│meс╣гu ca (тАж) rudr├нyeс╣гu.) Klein (DGRV I.54) calls this тАЬthe most anomalous position of ca within adjective plus noun syntagms.тАЭ This difficulty disappears if we take rudr├нyeс╣гu not as an adjective with st├│meс╣гu, but as a third term in the conjoined phrase: тАЬin the hymns, in the praises, and in the Rudriyans.тАЭ The ca is then correctly positioned in an X Y Z ca construction (on which see Klein DGRV I.86-91). The Rudriyans in question are the Maruts. It is important to note that the adj. rudr├нya- is almost never used of anyone or anything but the Maruts, and in the plural never of anything but the Maruts. It is also never used of hymns or praises. It is true that my interpr. produces disharmony in semantic class: two types of verbal products and a group of gods, but Indra does indeed get pleasure and strengthening both from human praises and from the Maruts, who stood by him at the Vс╣Ыtra battle. And my interpr. solves the ca placement problem and also allows rudr├нya- to refer to its accustomed referent.

A more intractable problem is how to interpr. the loc. relative pronouns in a and c. The standard tr. seem to take them (itтАЩs a little hard to tell) as embedded relatives with the loc. nouns (ukth├йс╣гu, etc.) belonging to the main clause whose predicate takes shape in p─Бda d. The published translation (JPB) takes ab as a separate sentence, supplying an impv. тАЬdelight!тАЭ as the main cl. verb, governing ukth├йс╣гu тАж rudr├нyeс╣гu ca and generated from the injunctive pf. c─Бk├бn of the rel. cl. This still leaves the y─Б╠Бsu cl. embedded, since the main clause in cd must include t├║bhy├йd that begins c, parallel to v─Бy├бve in d. Another wrinkle is the fact that the verbal predicate of this 2nd rel.

clause is not finite, but a predicated middle participle (whatever its exact derivational path) mandas─Бn├бс╕е (on which see comm. ad IV.3.6). In favor of the JPB solution is the fact that the y─Б╠Бsu rel. prn. has a clear antecedent in the main clause of cd: nom. pl.

et─Б╠Б(с╕е), but it is not clear whether masc. y├йс╣гu does. If we take the nominal loc. pls.

ukth├йс╣гu, etc., as belonging to the main clause, then it does. This seems to be the solution of the standard tr. (e.g., RenouтАЩs tenative тАЬparmi (?) les hymnes en lesquels tu te complais et parmi (?) les corps-de-louange rudriens тАжтАЭ I do not know the answer, though IтАЩm inclined to follow the standard tr., against the published translation, and take these masc. locatives as belonging to the main clause, with loc. relative clauses dependent on them, parallel to the fem. loc. in c. So, rather like Renou, тАЬAmidst the hymns, praises, and Rudriyans in which you take (have taken? injunc. pf.) delight, these (FEM. PL.), in which you are finding exhilaration, run forth to you тАжтАЭ As the just-produced tr. shows, yet another problem is the identity of the subject of the main clause and its verb sisrate. The subj. must be fem. because of the et─Б╠Б(с╕е) and it is either qualified as ┼Ыubhr─Б╠Бс╕е тАШresplendentтАЩ or compared to entities that are. The anomalous position of the simile particle n├б is, uneasily, compatible with either: тАЬresplendent like XesтАЭ or тАЬlike resplendent Xes.тАЭ Various solutions for the identity of the subject have been suggested. The published translation тАШwatersтАЩ seems the most likely, since 1) the verb means тАШrun forth, flowтАЩ, 2) the subj. must be fem. pl., 3) ┼Ыubhr├б- elsewhere characterizes waters and rivers, and 4) the waters were prominent in the immediately preceding vs., though not named, and rivers appear in 1d.

Identifying the referent of ┼Ыubhr─Б╠Бс╕е is complicated by the fact that this stem is the signature word of the next vs. _________ 04
The first two p─Бdas contain two exx. of predicated pres. participles, vardh├бyantaс╕е and d├бdh─Бn─Бс╕е, but unfortunately itтАЩs not clear what they are predicated of. Geldner, Renou, and the published translation supply тАЬwe,тАЭ which is a reasonable default, Witzel Got┼Н тАЬdiese Lobreden,тАЭ from 3a (which does not work because ukth├б- is neut. and the participles are masc.). In any case, the referents of these participles are not directly reflected in the rest of the verse (save perhaps for asm├й тАШfor us / among usтАЩ in c), and it seems best with the standard tr. to assume an abrupt syntactic division between ab and cd because the subject of ab must be plural, not sg., though the intrans./pass. part.

v─Бvс╣Ыdh─Бn├бс╕е and the adj. ┼Ыubhr├бс╕е in c show lexical and thematic continuity with the first hemistich.

JPB takes c as an independent nominal clause. IтАЩd be inclined, with the standard tr., to take it with d with the pf. part. v─Бvс╣Ыdh─Бn├бс╕е expressing anteriority and notional dependence: тАЬтАж having become strengthened, you should overwhelm тАжтАЭ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe are invigorating your brilliant strength (by our praises), and plural cing the thunderbolt in your hands; do you, Indra, radiant, increasing in strenght, and (encouraged) by the sun, overpower, for our (good), the servile people.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

And encouraged by the sun: d─Бs─лr vi┼Ыaс╕е s┼лryeс╣Зa sahy─Бс╕е = upakс╣гapayitr─лс╕е, or ─Бsur─лс╕е praj─Бс╕е, people interrupting religious rites,or the race of asuras;

S┼лryeс╣Зa = prerakeс╣Зa, urger, instrumental gator (used like an adjective

Jamison Brereton

Now (that we) are strengthening your resplendent explosiveness, are placing in your arms your resplendent mace,
resplendent are you, Indra, as you have become strong among us. Along with the sun, you should overcome the D─Бsa clans.

Griffith

We who add strength to thine own splendid vigour, laying within thine arms the splendid thunder-
With us mayst thou, O Indra, waxen splendid, with Surya overcome the Dasa races.

Geldner

Indem wir deinen gl├дnzenden Mut aufrichten und die gl├дnzende Keule in deine Arme legen - Wenn du Indra, der Gl├дnzende, dich bei uns aufgerichtet hast, sollst du die dasischen St├дmme mit der Sonne bezwingen.

Grassmann

Die schmucke Kraft nun lassen sie dir wachsen, den schmucken Blitz in deine Arme legend; Und schmuck bist Indra du von uns gekr├дftigt; die b├╢sen St├дmme schlage mit der Sonne.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, hero, you have slain by your prow the glorified Ahi, hidden privy in a cave, lurking in concealment, covered by the waters in which he was abiding, and arresting the rains in the sky.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The one placed in hiding, the hidden one hiding amid the waters, the wily one dwelling under cover
and blocking the waters and the heavenтАФ(that) serpent you smashed by your heroic deed, o champion.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda c is oddly conceived. The problem is the double object of the pf. part.

tastabhv─Б╠Бс╣Гsam, namely ap├│ dy─Б╠Бm тАЬthe waters (and) heaven.тАЭ The first, in a putative VP ap├│ тИЪstambh, is perfectly fine, and indeed perfectly fine as a description of Vс╣Ыtra.

Although тИЪstambh ordinarily means тАШprop up, make fastтАЩ, in the latter sense it can come to mean тАШstay, blockтАЩ, with rivers (bzw. waters) as obj. Cf. III.53.9 ├бstabhn─Бt s├нndhum arс╣Зav├бm тАЬhe stayed the river in flood,тАЭ depicting Vi┼Ыv─БmitraтАЩs feat in stopping the rivers to allow Sud─БsтАЩs forces to cross, presented at length in the famous hymn III.33. Also, with тИЪstambh in the passive, in VIII.96.18 tv├бс╣Г s├нndh┼лm╠Рasс╣Ыjas tastabh─Бn─Б╠Бn тАЬyou released the rivers, which had been blocked/stayed,тАЭ exactly of IndraтАЩs freeing the waters after smiting Vс╣Ыtra, as here. But тИЪstambh is far more common with dy─Б╠Бm as object; this VP means тАЬprop up heavenтАЭ and is regularly used of one of IndraтАЩs signature cosmogonic deed - including in this sequence of Indra hymns. Cf. in the next (very famous) hymn, II.12.2 y├│ dy─Б╠Бm ├бstabhn─Бt s├б jan─Бsa ├нndraс╕е тАЬwho propped up heaven, that, o peoples, is IndraтАЭ; II.15.2 dy─Б╠Бm astabh─Бyad bс╣Ыh├бntam тАЬhe propped up lofty heavenтАЭ; II.17.5 ├бstabhn─Бn m─Бy├бy─Б dy─Б╠Бm avasr├бsaс╕е тАЬwith his craft he propped up heaven (to keep it) from falling.тАЭ It is very strange to assign IndraтАЩs deed and its formulaic expression to Vс╣Ыtra. To rescue the phrase, Geldner suggests that тАЬheavenтАЭ stands for тАЬheavenтАЩs lightтАЭ; neither Oldenberg nor Renou (whose tr. in EVP XVII of course lacks notes) comments, nor Klein (DGRV 335), who tr. тАЬthe one blocking the waters (and) heaven.тАЭ Witzel Got┼Н tr. тАЬder dazu Wasser und Himmel befestigt hat,тАЭ with further glosses in the n.: тАЬmehrdeutig: der Wasser und Himmel gespreizt / zur Festung gemacht / festgebunden / paralysiert hatтАЭ - none of which helps with the anomaly of dy─Б╠Бm тИЪstambh in this context. I find it difficult to imagine that the audience (more alert than us Western commentators), hearing dy─Б╠Бс╣Г tastabhv─Б╠Бс╣Гsam, esp. in an Indra hymn, would not immediately associate it with the standard Indra formula and find the attribution of such a deed to Vс╣Ыtra (whom Indra will smash in the next p─Бda) disturbingтАФtwisting the perfectly acceptable ap├бс╕е тИЪstambh phrase in a disconcerting direction. But I donтАЩt quite know what to do with this. I would certainly not suggest that they then interpreted this participial phrase to refer to Indra - more that they were forced to rescue it by a semantic reconfiguration, perhaps like the one Geldner suggests – though nowhere else that I’m aware of is Vс╣Ыtra credited with blocking the light of heaven.

In any case, against the published translation, I would take the pf. part. as expressing anteriority - тАЬhaving blocked / who had blocked the waters and heaven.тАЭ

Griffith

Hero, thou slewest in thy valour Ahi concealed in depths, mysterious, great enchanter,
Dwelling enveloped deep within the waters, him who checked heaven and stayed the floods from flowing.

Den im Versteck befindlichen, sich versteckenden, in den Gew├дssern versteckten, verborgen hausenden, zauberischen, und der Wasser und Himmel festgebannt hatte, den Drachen erschlugst du Held mit Manneskraft.

Der sich versteckt in Wasserflut sich bergend, den listigen, verh├╝llten, der sich hinstreckt, Und der die Wasser fesselt und den Himmel, den Drachen schlugst mit M├дnnerkraft, o Held, du.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe glorify, Indra, your mighty (deeds) of old; we glorify your (more) recent exploits; we praise the thunderbolt shining in your arms, and we celebrate the horses, the signs of (Indra as) the sun.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The sing of (Indra as) the sun: hari s_ryasya ketu, the two horses the signs of the sun;

S┼лrya = instrumental gator or heroic, suс╣гс╣нu prerakasya; or, su-v─лryasya, as indicating Indra; or, Indra is identified with S┼лrya, s┼лry─Бtmanaс╕е indrasya

Jamison Brereton

Now I shall praise your ancient, great deeds, Indra, and we shall praise your present deeds.
I shall praise the eager mace in your arms. I shall praise your fallow bays, twin beacons of the sun.

Griffith

Indra, we laud thy great deeds wrought aforetime, we laud thine exploits later of achievement;
We laud the bolt that in thine arms lies eager; we laud thy two Bay Steeds, heralds of Surya.

Geldner

Ich will nun deine fr├╝heren gro├Яen Taten preisen, Indra, und wir wollen deine neueren Taten preisen. Ich will die willige Keule in deinen Armen preisen, ich will deine beiden Falben preisen, die zwei Strahlen der Sonne sind.

Grassmann

Wir wollen preisen deine alten Thaten, wir wollen preisen auch die neu vollbrachten; Den will’gen Blitz in deinen Armen preisen, dein F├╝chsepaar, der Sonne Fackeln, r├╝hmen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYour swift horses, Indra, have uttered a loud sound, announcing rain; the level earth anxiously expects its fall, as the gathering cloud has passed.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Now your two fallow bays, competing for the prize, Indra, have cried out their cry, dripping with ghee.
The land has spread out equally in all directions. Even the mountain, which was about to run, has come to rest.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The three augmented aorists in this vs. are striking, esp. because two of them are extremely marginal: the s-aor. seen in asv─Бrс╣гс╣н─Бm (тИЪsvar) is found otherwise in the RV only as 3rd sg. ├бsv─Бr in late X.148.5; ├бraс╣Гsta is the only form of this s-aor. in the RV. Both have well-attested 1st cl. present stems with the same meaning, and it is, at first, surprising in this narrative context that we donтАЩt find imperfects. But as Ian Hollenbaugh suggested to me, if we follow the interpr. of the hymn in the published introduction. and in Brereton 1985, whereby the apparent events of the mythic pastтАФthe spreading out of the earth, the coming to rest of the mountainтАФactually refer to the ritual here-andnow, esp. the establishment of the fire, then the augmented aorists will force an immediate past interpr. and therefore reveal the poetтАЩs intent behind the apparent recital of mythic events.

I would be inclined to take cid with sariс╣гy├бn, rather than with p├бrvataс╕е, hence тАЬthe mountain, though about to run, has come to rest,тАЭ rather than тАЬeven the mountain тАжтАЭ Note the use of the future participle to express past prospective value in subordination to a preterital main verb and see comm. ad 10b below.

Griffith

Indra, thy Bay Steeds showing forth their vigour have sent a loud cry out that droppeth fatness.
The earth hath spread herself in all her fulness: the cloud that was about to move hath rested.

Geldner

Dein um den Preis laufendes Falbenpaar hat sein schmalztriefendes Get├╢se ert├╢nen lassen. Die Erde hat sich gleichm├д├Яig ausgebreitet, selbst der Berg, der davonlaufen wollte, ist stillgestanden.

Grassmann

Dein F├╝chsepaar, o Indra, kr├дftig eilend liess rauschen nun ein Rauschen, wie wenn Fett trieft; Auf einmal that sich auf die weite Erde; der Wolkenberg auch jauchzte, Wasser str├╢mend.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe cloud, not heedless (of its office), is suspended (in the sky); resonant with maternal (waters), it has spread about; (the winds), augmenting the sound in the distant horizon; have promulgated the voice uttered by Indra.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The mountain, never faltering, has been set down. Bellowing with its mothers, it roared.
Making their voice strong to the furthest distance, they [=priests or Maruts?] spread out the vein [=the sap-rich soma stalk or a
watercourse?] that was impelled by Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

After the three augmented aorists in the previous vs. and with akr─Бn in p─Бda b, the injunctive s─Бdi in p─Бda a is a little surprising, esp. since this p─Бda seems to describe the same action as 7d. I wonder whether the poet is playing a trick: the negated participle ├бprayuchan almost seems to have the augment we expect in *as─Бdi but transposed to the next word (and of course etymologically and functionally quite distinct). Note that ├бprayuchan occupies the same metrical position as ├бprathiс╣гс╣нa in 7c (the immediately preceding hemistich) and shares the same first two syllables.

The s-aor. akr─Бс╣З in b should be tr. тАЬhas roaredтАЭ to match the other augmented aorists in the immediate context.

The lexeme n├н тИЪprath occurs only here in the RV and, at least according to Mon.-Wms., in all of Sanskrit. This isolation makes it all the more difficult to figure out what is going on in p─Бda d, since the reference of the almost equally isolated dham├бni- is unclear. Note the placement of the preverb n├н after the verb paprathan at the end of the verse, an almost mirror image of the opening of the vs. n├н p├бrvataс╕е.

This vs.-final paprathan n├н is also echoed by the end of the 1st hemistich in the next vs. asphuran n├нс╕е. Both verbs precede their preverbs, but despite having apparently identical endings, -an, the first is a real 3rd pl. -an, where asphuran represents 3rd sg. asphurat in sandhi.

Griffith

Down, never ceasing, hath the rain-cloud settled: bellowing, it hath wandered with the Mothers.
Swelling the roar in the far distant limits, they have spread wide the blast sent forth by Indra.

Geldner

Der Berg setzte sich fest, nicht von der Stelle gehend; in das Gebl├╢ke der M├╝tter einstimmend hat er sein Gebr├╝ll erhoben. In die Ferne, bis zum anderen Ende den Ton verst├дrkend verbreiteten sie das von Indra entsandte Geblase weiter.

Grassmann

Der Wolkenberg liess unges├дumt sich nieder, er br├╝llte jauchzend mit der Flut, den M├╝ttern; Zum fernen Erdrand, das Get├╢n verst├дrkend, verbreiten sie den Ton, den Indra anblies.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe thunderbolt of the showerer roared aloud, when (Indra), the friend of man, sought to slay the enemy of mankind. Drinking the Soma, he (Indra), baffled the devices of the guileful D─Бnava.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The friend of man sought to: am─Бnuс╣гam yan m─Бnuс╣гo nij┼лrv─Бt, when the man, or the benefactor of man, manuс╣гy─Бс╣З─Бm hitak─Бr─л, destroyed the no-man (manuс╣гy─Бс╣Зam rahitam); i.e. the manuс╣гy─Бс╣З─Бm ahitam, not friendly to man

Jamison Brereton

The mace of him, the bull, bellowed again and again when (Indra), the ally of Manu, was about to grind down (Vr╠еtra), the enemy of Manu. He brought low the wiles of the wily son of D─Бnu, when he had drunk of the pressed soma.

Jamison Brereton Notes

It is unusual to find a subjunctive nij┼л╠Бrv─Бt in a subord. clause whose main cl. has an imperfect intensive (├бrorav─лt). The published translation renders it as тАЬwas about to grind downтАЭ – this seems pretty close to target, though IтАЩd probably substitute rather тАЬwas going toтАЭ – a past prospective. S─Бyaс╣Зa. simply glosses with a desiderative jigh─Бс╣Гsat─лty arthaс╕е. Of course, the -─Бt isnтАЩt metrically guaranteed and could have been introduced from v├бjr─Бt at the end of 9d, so it is possible that the form was simply injunc. n├нj┼л╠Бrvat. Nonetheless, though the usage of the subjunctive here is unusual, I think it can be reconciled with the function of the subjunctive more generally. Note that its function is very much parallel to that of the future participle sariс╣гy├бn in 7d.

The pf. part. papiv─Б╠Бn would be better tr. тАЬafter having drunk.тАЭ Both nij┼л╠Бrv─Бt and papiv─Б╠Бn are means of indicating anteriority here.

Griffith

Loud roared the mighty Hero’s bolt of thunder, when he, the Friend of man, burnt up the monster,
And, having drunk his fill of flowing Soma, baffled the guileful Danava’s devices.

Geldner

Es br├╝llte seine, des Bullen, Keule, da├Я der Menschliche den Unmenschen verzehren solle. Er brachte die Zaubereien des zauberischen Danava zu Fall, nachdem er Soma getrunken hatte.

Grassmann

Laut krachte seine Waffe, als der starke, der Menschenfreund, den Menschenfeind verbrannte; Des zauberhaften D├дmons Listen schlug er zu Boden, als vom Safte er getrunken.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDrink, hero, Indra, drink the Soma;may the exhilarating juices delight you; may they, distending your flanks, augment (your prowess), and in this manner may the replenishing effused libation satisfy Indra.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Drink and drink the soma, o Indra, our champion! Let the exhilarating soma-pressings exhilarate you.
As they fill your cheeks, let them strengthen you. When properly pressed among the Paura, (the soma) has helped Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In d JPB takes paur├б as paur├й out of sandhi, as a PN. In VIII.61.6 I take it as тАШmultiplierтАЩ (of Indra) in a pun with purukс╣Ы╠Бt-. In VIII.50.5 a clear loc. shows the sense that JPB wants. In V.74.4 there are three exx., one apparently a PN, the other also apparently a pun on puru- (JPB tr. тАШmuchnessтАЩ). IтАЩd be inclined here to take it in non-PN name fashion, either as loc. тАЬin its muchnessтАЭ or modifying soma: тАЬsoma multipliedтАЭ (to puru) or perhaps more likely, given pс╣Ыс╣З├бntaс╕е in c, тАШfillingтАЩ or тАШin its fullnessтАЩ.

Griffith

Drink thou, O Hero Indra, drink the Soma; let the joy-giving juices make thee joyful.
They, filling both thy flanks, shall swell thy vigour. The juice that satisfies hath helped Indra.

Geldner

Trink, trink doch, tapferer Indra, den Soma ! Dich sollen die berauschenden Pre├Яtr├дnke berauschen. Deine Seiten f├╝llend sollen sie dich st├дrken. Der also gepre├Яte F├╝ller hat fr├╝her dem Indra geholfen.

Grassmann

O trinke, trinke, Indra, Held, den Soma, berauschen m├╢gen dich des Rausches Tr├дnke, Den Bauch dir f├╝llend m├╢gen sie dich st├дrken; der wohlgebraute F├╝ller labte Indra.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay we, your pious (worshipper), abide in you; approaching you with devotion, may we enjoy (the reward of) our adoration; desirous of protection, we meditate your glorification; may we ever be (thought worthy) of the gift of your treasures.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

We inspired poets have abided by you, Indra. Serving according to the truth, we would gain insight.
Seeking your help, we would create for ourselves a proclamation of your praise. On this very day, we would be those to be given wealth by you.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I would tr. dh─лmahi in c as тАШacquireтАЩ – the idea being that we want to get a pr├б┼Ыasti- from our actions performed with IndraтАЩs help.

Griffith

Singers have we become with thee, O Indra: may we serve duly and prepare devotion.
Seeking thy help we meditate thy praises: may we at once enjoy thy gift of riches.

Geldner

Bei dir, Indra, haben wir Redekundigen Zuflucht gesucht. Wir wollen Gewinn von der Dichtung haben, indem wir sie richtig pflegen. Um Gunst bittend m├╢chten wir Anerkennung finden, wir m├╢chten alsbald dir zum Schenken von Reichtum ausersehen sein.

Grassmann

Wir S├дnger sind, o Indra, ganz dein eigen, lasst Andacht weih’n uns, wie es recht, dich ehrend, Und deine Huld uns, Gunst begehrend, preisen; stets sei uns Theil an deiner G├╝terspende.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay we, (through) your (favour), Indra, be such as those are, who, desirous of your protection, augment (by their praises) your vigour; divine (Indra), you grant the wealth which we desire, (the source of) great power and of (numerous) progeny.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Indra, might we be those of yours who are accompanied by your help, since, seeking your help, we make your nourishment strong.
Grant us the most explosive wealth in which we will delight, o godтАФ that consisting of heroic men.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda b contains another predicated pres. participle, vardh├бyantaс╕е.

Griffith

May we be thine, such by thy help, O Indra, as swell thy vigour while they seek thy favour.
Give us, thou God, the riches that we long for, most powerful, with stare of noble children.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou grant a habitation; you grant friends; you grant us, Indra, the strength of the Maruts; the winds, who, propitious and exulting, drink copiously of the first offering (of the Soma).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The winds: v─Бyavaс╕е is used honorifically for v─Бyu, in the singular, who is the first drinker of the Soma: vayur hi somasya agrap─Б

Jamison Brereton

Grant us peaceful dwelling. Grant us alliance. Grant us a Marutian warrior band, o Indra.
And they who jointly are finding exhilarationтАФ(those) Winds drink the first offering.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda c contains yet another predicated pres. part., mandas─Бn─Б╠Бс╕е. It cannot belong with the main cl. verb in d, p─Бnti, because it modifies a rel. prn. y├й and p─Бnti is unaccented. The primary ending on p─Бnti is disturbing: the context requires a connection with тИЪp─Б тАШdrinkтАЩ, but that root forms a root aorist. For another such form see I.134.5 and comm. ad loc.

Griffith

Give us a friend, give us an habitation; Indra, give us the company of Maruts,
And those whose minds accord with theirs, the Vayus, who drink the first libation of the Soma.

Geldner

Schenk uns Wohnung, schenk uns den Mitra, schenk uns die marutische Heeresmacht, o Indra, und alle, die eintr├дchtig mit dir sich berauschen: Die Vayu┬┤s trinken den ersten Reihen des Soma vor.

Grassmann

Gieb sichern Sitz und schenke einen Freund uns, und send’, o Indra, uns die Marutscharen, Und die vereinten Winde, die voll Freude des Opfers erste Spende gern geniessen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLet those in whom you are delighted repair (to the libation), and do you, Indra, confiding, drink the satiating Soma; liberator (from evil), associated with the mighty and adorable (Maruts), augment our prosperity, and (that of) heaven.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Let those in whom you are: may those Maruts or those Soma, in which you delight; associated with the mighty: asm─Бntsu pс╣Ыtsv─Б tarutr─Б avardhayo dy─Бm bс╣Ыhadbhir arkaiс╕е: pс╣Ыtsu qualified avardhaya, increase; i.e. with children, cattle, and the like; in consequence of which prosperous condition, men can offer sacrifices, to heaven to thrive;

Arkaiс╕е = arcan─лyaiс╕е, to be adored (the Maruts)

Jamison Brereton

Now let just those (soma juices) pursue youтАФthose among whom (you) are becoming exhilarated. Steadfastly drink our soma to your satisfaction, Indra.
(Be) near to us in battles, o surpassing one. You have strengthened
heaven through lofty chants.

Geldner suggests the impv. vardhaya. It would also be possible simply to read ├бvardhayaс╕е with both p─Бdas: тАЬyou have strengthened us in battles (and) have strengthened heaven тАжтАЭ]

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLiberator (from evil), they who worship you, the giver of happiness, with holy hymns, quickly become great; they who strew the sacred grass (in honour of you) are protected by you, and, together with their famiies, obtain (abundant) food.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Now just those lofty ones [=priests], who will try to win your favor, o you surpassing one, either by their hymns
or in strewing the ritual grass that provides (you) a dwelling place, have come to the prize, helped just by you, Indra.

Griffith

Great, verily, are they, O thou Protector, who by their songs of praise have won the blessing.
They who strew sacred grass to be thy dwelling, helped by thee have got them strength, O Indra.

Geldner

Gro├Я sind f├╝rwahr nur die, die etwa durch Loblieder deine Gunst gewinnen k├╢nnen, du ├Ьberwinder, wenn sie das Platz bietende Barhis auslegen. Mit deinem Beistand, o Indra, sind sie zu Sieg gelangt.

Grassmann

Die edlen M├дnner, welche jetzt, o Retter, durch Andachtsspr├╝che deine Gunst gewannen, Und die zum Sitzen dir das Lager streuten, durch dich, o Indra, kamen die zum Reichthum.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗрд╢реВрд░ рдмрд▓рд╡рдиреНрдирд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░ рдЙрдЧреНрд░реЗрд╖реБрдЙрджреНрдЧреВрд░реНрдгреЗрд╖реБрдмрд╣реБрд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╡рддреНрд╕реБрддреНрд░рд┐рдХрджреНрд░реБрдХреЗрд╖реБрдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рд░реНрдЧреМрд░рд╛рдпреБрд░рд┐рддреНрдпреЗрддрдиреНрдирд╛рдордХреЗрд╖реБ рдЖрднрд┐рдкреНрд▓рд╡рд┐рдХреЗрд╖реНрд╡рд╣рд╕реНрд╕реБрдордиреНрджрд╕рд╛рдиреЛрд╣реГрд╖реНрдпрдиреН рдиреБрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдВрд╕реЛрдордореНрдкрд╛рд╣рд┐рдкрд┐рдм рдЗрджрд┐рддрд┐рдкреВрд░рдгрдГ рддрддрдГ рдкреНрд░реАрдгрд╛рдирдГ рд╕реЛрдордкрд╛рдиреЗ- рдирдкреНрд░реАрддреЛрднрд╡рдиреН рд╢реНрдорд╢реНрд░реБрд╖реБрд▓рд┐рдкреНрддрдВрд╕реЛрдордореНрдкреНрд░рджреЛрдзреБрд╡рддреН рдзреВрдЮреНрдХрдореНрдкрдиреЗ рдпрдЩреНрд▓реБрдЧрдиреНрддрд╕реНрдпрд╢рддрд░рд┐рд░реВрдкрдореН рдкреБрдирдГрдкреБрдирд░реНрдзреБрдиреНрд╡рдиреН рд╕реБрддрд╕реНрдпрд╛- рднрд┐рд╖реБрддрд╕реНрдпрдкреАрддрд┐рдореНрдкрд╛рдирдореБрджреНрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрд╣рд░рд┐рднреНрдпрд╛рдорд╢реНрд╡рд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВрдпреБрдХреНрддрдГ рд╕рдиреН рдпрд╛рд╣рд┐рдЧрдЪреНрдЫ рее резрен рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, hero, exulting in the solemn Trikadruka rites quaff the Soma, and repeatedly shaking it from your beard, repair, well plural ased with your steeds, to the drinking of the effused libation.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Trikadruka rites: these denote three days, or celebrations of the ceremonial, termed abhiplava; abhiplavikeс╣гu ahaс╕е su: these are, jyotiс╣г, gauс╕е, ─Бyus; the text designates them as ugreс╣гu, fierce, angry; but here, ugra = having many praises and prayers, bahu stotra ┼Ыastravat

Jamison Brereton

Now, finding exhilaration among just these powerful (soma drops), o champion, drink the soma among the Trikadrukas [=the
Maruts?], Indra,
again and again shaking out (the soma) in your beard, becoming
pleased. Travel to the soma-drinking with your two fallow bays.

Griffith

Upon the great Trikadruka days, Hero, rejoicing thee, O Indra, drink the Soma.
Come with Bay Steeds to drink of libation, shaking the drops from out thy beard, contented.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЙрдЧреНрд░реЗрд╖реБ) рддреЗрдЬрд╕реНрд╡рд┐рд╖реБ (рдЗрддреН) рдПрд╡ (рдиреБ) рд╕рджреНрдпрдГ (рд╢реВрд░) рджреБрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рдХ (рдордиреНрджрд╕рд╛рдирдГ) рдХрд╛рдордпрдорд╛рдирдГ (рддреНрд░рд┐рдХрджреНрд░реБрдХреЗрд╖реБ) рддреНрд░реАрдгрд┐ рдХрджреНрд░реБрдХрд╛рдгрд┐ рд╢рд░реАрд░рд╛рддреНрдордордирдГрдкреАрдбрдирд╛рдирд┐ рдпреЗрд╖реБ рддреЗрд╖реБ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░реЗрд╖реБ (рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐) (рд╕реЛрдордореН) рдорд╣реМрд╖рдзрд┐рдЧрдгрдореН (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рд╡реИрджреНрдпрдХрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд┐рддреН (рдкреНрд░рджреЛрдзреБрд╡рддреН) рдкреНрд░рдХреГрд╖реНрдЯрддрдпрд╛ рдХрдореНрдкрдпрдиреН (рд╢реНрдорд╢реНрд░реБрд╖реБ) рдЪрд┐рдмреБрдХрд╛рджрд┐рд╖реБ (рдкреНрд░реАрдгрд╛рдирдГ) рддрд░реНрдкрдпрдиреН (рдпрд╛рд╣рд┐) рдЧрдЪреНрдЫ (рд╣рд░рд┐рднреНрдпрд╛рдореН) рд╕реБрд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдорд╢реНрд╡рд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдореН (рд╕реБрддрд╕реНрдп) рдирд┐рд╖реНрдкрдиреНрдирд╕реНрдп (рдкреАрддрд┐рдореН) рдкрд╛рдирдореН реерезренрее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

тАЬIndra, hero, keep up the strength wherewith you have crushed Vс╣Ыtra, the spider-like son of D─Бnu, and let open the light to the ─Аrya; the Dasyu has been set aside on your left hand.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The spider-like son of D─Бnu: d─Бnum aurс╣Зav─Бbham: aurс╣Зav─Бbham = aurс╣Зan─Бbham;

Aurс╣Зa = a spider;

─Аbha = resembling

Jamison Brereton

Take to yourself the vast power, o champion, by which you cut down Vr╠еtra, the son of D─Бnu, that son of a spider!
You uncovered the light for the ─Аrya; the Dasyu has been set down to the left, Indra.

Griffith

Hero, assume the might wherewith thou clavest Vrtra piecemeal, the Danava Aurnavabha.
Thou hast disclosed the light to light the Arya: on thy left hand, O Indra, sank the Dasyu.

тАЬLet us honour those men, who, through your protection, surpass all their rivals, as the Dasyus (are surpassed) by the Arya; this (have you wrought) for us; you have slain Vi┼Ыvar┼лpa, the son of Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б, through friendship of Trita.тАЭ

Trita: in this and next hymn, he is referred to as a maharс╣гi

We would win!тАФwe who by your help are overcoming all rivals, the Dasyus along with the ─Аrya.

Our gain was that to Trta of our party thou gavest up Tvastar’s son Visvarupa.

English translation:

тАЬInvigorated (by the libation) of the exulting Trita, offering you the Soma, you have annihilated Arbuda; Indra, aided by the Aс╣Еgirasa, has whirled round his bolt, as the tun turns round his wheel, and slain Bala.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

As the sun turns round his wheel: s┼лryo na cakram; if na is used in the negative sense, the phrase means: when the sun did not turn his wheel or stool still through fear of the asura; or, that Indra whirled the wheel like the sun, having taken one of the wheels of the sun’s chariot as a weapon against Bala

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThat opulent donation, which proceeds, Indra, from you, assuredly bestows upon him who praises you the boon (which he desires); grant it to us, your prisers; do not you, who are the object of adoration, disregard (our prayer); so that, blessed with worthy descendants, we may glorify you at this sacrifice.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Do not you who are: m─Бti dhag bhago no = bhajantyastvam asm─Бkam k─Бm─Бn m─Б dh─Бkс╣г─лс╕е, you who are adorable, consumenot our desires; bhago no astu = may fortune be to us (Nirukta 1.7)

Jamison Brereton

Now should the generous priestly gift yield your boon for the singer as its milk, Indra.
Exert yourself for the praise singers. Let fortune not pass us by. тАУ May we speak loftily at the ritual distribution, in possession of good
heroes.

Griffith

Now let that wealthy Cow of thine, O Indra, yield in return a boon to him who lauds thee.
Give to thy praisers: let not fortune fail us. Loud may we speak, with brave men, in the assembly.

Geldner

Nun soll diese deine reichliche Lohngabe, o Indra, dem S├дnger nach Wunsch ergiebig sein. Suche den S├дngern zu n├╝tzen; das Gl├╝ck soll nicht an uns vor├╝bergehen. - Wir m├╢chten das gro├Яe Wort f├╝hren als Meister in der Weisheit.

Grassmann

Wohlan, es locke diese reiche Gabe dir ab, o Indra, was der S├дnger w├╝nschet; Den Preisern spende, k├╝rze nicht den Antheil. Lasst laut im Chore bei dem Fest uns singen.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рджреЗрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ ! рдЬрд┐рди (рддреЗ) рдЖрдкрдХреА (рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрд╛) рдмрд▓ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реА (рдордШреЛрдиреА) рдкрд░рдордкреВрдЬрд┐рдд рдзрдирдпреБрдХреНрдд рдиреАрддрд┐ (рдЬрд░рд┐рддреНрд░реЗ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдХреА рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рд╡рд░рдореН) рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрда рдХреЛ (рдиреВрдирдореН) рдирд┐рд╢реНрдЪрдп рд╕реЗ (рдкреНрд░рддрд┐,рджреБрд╣реАрдпрддреН) рдкреВрд░рд╛ рдХрд░рддреА рд╣реБрдИ (рд╕реНрддреЛрддреГрднреНрдпрдГ) рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖) рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рджреЗрддреА рд╣реИ (рдорд╛,рдЕрддрд┐,рдзрдХреН) рдирд╣реАрдВ рдЕрддреАрд╡ рдХрд┐рд╕реА рдХреЛ рджрд╣рддреА рдирд╣реАрдВ рдХрд╖реНрдЯ рджреЗрддреА (рд╕рд╛) рд╡рд╣ (рдирдГ) рд╣рдорд╛рд░реЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рдмреГрд╣рджреНрднрдЧрдГ) рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддреГрдд рдзрди рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░рд╛рддреА рд╣реИ, рдЙрд╕ рдиреАрддрд┐ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрдХрд░, (рд╕реБрд╡реАрд░рд╛рдГ) рд╕реБрдиреНрджрд░ рд╡реАрд░рдЬрди рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧ (рд╡рд┐рджрдереЗ) рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдо рдореЗрдВ (рд╡рджреЗрдо) рдХрд╣реЗрдВ рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рдФрд░реЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ рджреЗрдВ реереирезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ рд╕рдмрдХреЛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рджреЗрдиреЗ рдФрд░ рд╕рддреНрдпреЛрдкрджреЗрд╢ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ рдмрд╣реБрдд рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрда рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрд╛ рджреЗрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╣реЛрдХрд░ рд╢реВрд░рд╡реАрд░ рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ реереирезрее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рд░рд╛рдЬрдзрд░реНрдо рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдФрд░ рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдкрддрд┐ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдкрд┐рдЫрд▓реЗ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рд╣реИ, рдпрд╣ рдЬрд╛рдирдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее рдпрд╣ рджреВрд╕рд░реЗ рдордгреНрдбрд▓ рдореЗрдВ рдЧреНрдпрд╛рд░рд╣рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдкреНрд░рдердо рдЕрдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХ рдФрд░ рдЫрдард╛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рдпрд╕реНрдп рддреЗ рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрд╛ рдордШреЛрдиреА рдиреАрддрд┐рд░реНрдЬрд░рд┐рддреНрд░реЗ рд╡рд░рдВ рд╕реБрдЦрдВ рдиреВрдирдВ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐ рджреБрд╣реАрдпрддреНрд╕реНрддреЛрддреГрднреНрдпрдГ рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖ рдорд╛рддрд┐рдзрдХреН рд╕рд╛ рдиреЛ рдмреГрд╣рджреНрднрдЧрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдпрддрд┐ рддрд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдп рд╕реБрд╡реАрд░рд╛ рд╡рдпрдВ рд╡рд┐рджрдереЗ рд╡рджреЗрдо реереирезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд░реНрд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдиреВрдирдореН) рдирд┐рд╢реНрдЪрд┐рддрдореН (рд╕рд╛) рд╡рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрдорд╛рдгрд╛ (рддреЗ) рддрд╡ (рдкреНрд░рддрд┐) (рд╡рд░рдореН) рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрдардореН (рдЬрд░рд┐рддреНрд░реЗ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╕реНрддрд╛рд╡рдХрд╛рдп (рджреБрд╣реАрдпрддреН) рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкрд╛рджрдпрдиреН (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рджрд╛рддрдГ (рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрд╛) рдмрд▓рдХрд╛рд░рд┐рдгреА (рдордШреЛрдиреА) рдкрд░рдордкреВрдЬрд┐рддрдзрдирдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛ (рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖) рдЕрдиреБрд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддрд┐ (рд╕реНрддреЛрддреГрднреНрдпрдГ) (рдорд╛) рдирд┐рд╖реЗрдзреЗ (рдкреНрд░рддрд┐) (рдзрдХреН) рджрд╣рддрд┐ (рднрдЧрдГ) рдзрдирдореН (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдореН (рдмреГрд╣рддреН) рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддреАрд░реНрдгрдореН (рд╡рджреЗрдо) (рд╡рд┐рджрдереЗ) рд╕рдЩреНрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗ (рд╕реБрд╡реАрд░рд╛рдГ) рд╢реЛрднрдирд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рддреЗ рд╡реАрд░рд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рддреЗ реереирезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпреЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рджрд╛рддреНрд░реЗ рд╕рддреНрдпреЛрдкрджреЗрд╢рдХрд░реНрддреНрд░реЗ рдкреБрд╖реНрдХрд▓рд╛рдВ рд╡рд░рд╛рдВ рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрд╛рдВ рджрджрддрд┐ рддреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕реЛ рднреВрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╢реВрд░рд╡реАрд░рд╛ рдЬрд╛рдпрдиреНрддреЗ реереирезрее рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрд╕реВрдХреНрддреЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрдзрд░реНрдорд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рддреНрд╕реЗрдирд╛рдкрддрд┐рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрдордгреНрдбрд▓реЗ рдПрдХрд╛рджрд╢рдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рдкреНрд░рдердореЛрд╜рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХрдГ рд╖рд╖реНрдареЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдВрдирд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рджреЗрдгрд╛рд▒реНрдпрд╛ рд╡ рд╕рддреНрдпреЛрдкрджреЗрд╢ рдХрд░рдгрд╛рд▒реНрдпрд╛рдВрдирд╛ рдЙрддреНрдХреГрд╖реНрдЯ рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрд╛ рджреЗрддрд╛рдд рддреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рди рд╡ рд╢реВрд░рд╡реАрд░ рдЕрд╕рддрд╛рдд. рее реирез рее
